## Important

This repository should be used as the **ported TradingView REST API + TypeScript implementation**.

Do not use the old Python package for new integrations in this repo.
- The old GitHub Python library was used only for porting/parity reference.
- Use REST endpoints: `POST /api/v1/scan`, `POST /api/v1/scan/raw`, `GET /api/v1/symbol-search/v3`, `POST /api/v1/metainfo/:market`, `GET /api/v1/metadata/*`
- Use docs: `docs/rest-api-guide.md`
- Use TS client: `packages/client`

The old Python implementation is kept only for porting parity and audits.

## Overview (REST API Port)

Quick start for local API server:

```bash
npm ci
npm run generate:metadata
npm --workspace @tv-screener/api run dev
```

### Key Features

- **Markets**: Stocks, crypto, forex, CFDs, futures, bonds, and more.
- **3000+ Data Fields**: OHLC data, technical indicators, fundamental metrics (e.g. P/E, EPS), and even internal TradingView-only fields.
- **Timeframes**: Use 1m, 5m, 15m, 30m, 1h, 2h, 4h, 1d, 1w, and 1mo — freely mix timeframes per field, no subscription required.
- **Filtering**: SQL-like syntax with full support for `AND`/`OR` logic.


### Links

- [REST API Guide](docs/rest-api-guide.md)
- [Python Deprecation Policy](docs/python-deprecation.md)
- [GitHub Repository](https://github.com/shner-elmo/TradingView-Screener)
- [Documentation](https://shner-elmo.github.io/TradingView-Screener/3.0.0/tradingview_screener.html)
- [Fields](https://shner-elmo.github.io/TradingView-Screener/fields/stocks.html)
- [Screeners](https://shner-elmo.github.io/TradingView-Screener/screeners/stocks/america.html)

Note that throughout the documentation, "field" and "column" are used interchangeably.
Same with "Scanner" and "Screener".

## Legacy Python Reference (Do Not Use For New Integrations)

The content below is retained only as migration/parity reference from the original Python library.
For new usage in this repo, use the REST API sections further below.

Legacy Python example:

```python
from tradingview_screener import Query

x = (Query()
 .select('name', 'close', 'volume', 'market_cap_basic')
 .get_scanner_data())
print(x)
```

**Output:**

```
(17580,
          ticker  name   close     volume  market_cap_basic
 0   NASDAQ:NVDA  NVDA  127.25  298220762      3.130350e+12
 1      AMEX:SPY   SPY  558.70   33701795               NaN
 2   NASDAQ:TSLA  TSLA  221.10   73869589      7.063350e+11
 3    NASDAQ:QQQ   QQQ  480.26   29102854               NaN
 4    NASDAQ:AMD   AMD  156.40   76693809      2.531306e+11
 ..          ...   ...     ...        ...               ...
 45   NASDAQ:PDD   PDD  144.22    8653323      2.007628e+11
 46     NYSE:JPM   JPM  214.52    5639973      6.103447e+11
 47     NYSE:JNJ   JNJ  160.16    7274621      3.855442e+11
 48  NASDAQ:SQQQ  SQQQ    7.99  139721164               NaN
 49  NASDAQ:ASTS  ASTS   34.32   32361315      9.245616e+09
 
 [50 rows x 5 columns])
```

By default, the result is limited to 50 rows. You can adjust this limit, but be mindful of server load and potential
bans.

A more advanced query:

```python
from tradingview_screener import Query, col

(Query()
 .select('name', 'close', 'close|1', 'close|5', 'volume', 'relative_volume_10d_calc')
 .where(
     col('market_cap_basic').between(1_000_000, 50_000_000),
     col('relative_volume_10d_calc') > 1.2,
     col('MACD.macd|1') >= col('MACD.signal|1')  # 1 minute MACD
 )
 .order_by('volume', ascending=False)
 .offset(5)
 .limit(25)
 .get_scanner_data())
```

<br>
Note that some fields (usually prices and indicators) have multiple timeframes that you can choose from, for example:

| Timeframe | Column |
|---|---|
| 1 Minute | `close\|1` |
| 5 Minutes | `close\|5` |
| 15 Minutes | `close\|15` |
| 30 Minutes | `close\|30` |
| 1 Hour | `close\|60` |
| 2 Hours | `close\|120` |
| 4 Hours | `close\|240` |
| 1 Day | `close` |
| 1 Week | `close\|1W` |
| 1 Month | `close\|1M` |

## Real-Time Data Access

To access real-time data, you need to pass your session cookies, as even free real-time data requires authentication.

### Verify Update Mode

You can run this query to get an overview on the `update_mode` you get for each exchange:
```python
from tradingview_screener import Query

_, df = Query().select('exchange', 'update_mode').limit(1_000_000).get_scanner_data()
df = df.groupby('exchange')['update_mode'].value_counts()
print(df)
```
```
exchange  update_mode          
AMEX      delayed_streaming_900    3255
NASDAQ    delayed_streaming_900    4294
NYSE      delayed_streaming_900    2863
OTC       delayed_streaming_900    7129
```

### Using rookiepy

`rookiepy` is a library that loads the cookies from your local browser.
So if you are logged in on Chrome (or whatever browser you use), it will use the same session.

1. Install `rookiepy`:

    ```bash
    pip install rookiepy
    ```

2. Load the cookies:

    ```python
    import rookiepy
    cookies = rookiepy.to_cookiejar(rookiepy.chrome(['.tradingview.com']))  # replace chrome() with your browser
    ```

3. Pass the cookies when querying:

    ```python
    Query().get_scanner_data(cookies=cookies)
    ```

Now, if you re-run the update mode check:

```python
_, df = Query().select('exchange', 'update_mode').limit(1_000_000).get_scanner_data(cookies=cookies)
df = df.groupby('exchange')['update_mode'].value_counts()
print(df)
```
```
exchange  update_mode          
AMEX      streaming                3256
NASDAQ    streaming                4286
NYSE      streaming                2860
OTC       delayed_streaming_900    7175
```
We now get live-data for all exchanges except `OTC` (because my subscription dosent include live-data for OTC tickers).


### Other Ways For Loading Cookies

<details>
<summary>Extract Cookies Manually</summary>

1. Go to [TradingView](https://www.tradingview.com)
2. Open the developer tools (`Ctrl + Shift + I`)
3. Navigate to the `Application` tab.
4. Go to `Storage > Cookies > https://www.tradingview.com/`
5. Copy the value of `sessionid`
6. Pass it in your query:

    ```python
    cookies = {'sessionid': '<your-session-id>'}
    Query().get_scanner_data(cookies=cookies)
    ```

</details>


<details>
<summary>Authenticate via API</summary>

While it's possible to authenticate directly via API, TradingView has restrictions on login frequency, which may result
in CAPTCHA requests and account flagging (meaning this method won't work again until the cooldown expires and the CAPTCHA
is gone).  
If you wish to proceed, here’s how:

```python
from http.cookiejar import CookieJar

import requests
from tradingview_screener import Query


def authenticate(username: str, password: str) -> CookieJar:
    session = requests.Session()
    r = session.post(
       'https://www.tradingview.com/accounts/signin/', 
       headers={'User-Agent': 'Mozilla/5.0', 'Referer': 'https://www.tradingview.com'}, 
       data={'username': username, 'password': password, 'remember': 'on'}, 
       timeout=60,
    )
    r.raise_for_status()
    if r.json().get('error'):
        raise Exception(f'Failed to authenticate: \n{r.json()}')
    return session.cookies


cookies = authenticate('<your-username-or-email>', '<your-password>')
Query().get_scanner_data(cookies=cookies)
```

</details>

## Comparison to Similar Packages

Unlike other Python libraries that have specific features like extracting the sentiment, or what not.
This package is but a (low-level) wrapper around TradingView's `/screener` API endpoint.

It merely documents the endpoint, by listing all the functions and operations available, the different fields you can 
use, the markets, instruments (even some that you wont find on TradingView's website), and so on.

This library is also a wrapper that makes it easier to generate those verbose JSON payloads.


## Robustness & Longevity

This package is designed to be future-proof. There are no hard-coded values in the package, all fields/columns and markets are documented on the website, which is updated
daily via a GitHub Actions script.

## How It Works

When using methods like `select()` or `where()`, the `Query` object constructs a dictionary representing the API
request. Here’s an example of the dictionary generated:

```python
{
    'markets': ['america'],
    'symbols': {'query': {'types': []}, 'tickers': []},
    'options': {'lang': 'en'},
    'columns': ['name', 'close', 'volume', 'relative_volume_10d_calc'],
    'sort': {'sortBy': 'volume', 'sortOrder': 'desc'},
    'range': [5, 25],
    'filter': [
        {'left': 'market_cap_basic', 'operation': 'in_range', 'right': [1000000, 50000000]},
        {'left': 'relative_volume_10d_calc', 'operation': 'greater', 'right': 1.2},
        {'left': 'MACD.macd', 'operation': 'egreater', 'right': 'MACD.signal'},
    ],
}
```

The `get_scanner_data()` method sends this dictionary as a JSON payload to the TradingView API,
allowing you to query data using SQL-like syntax without knowing the specifics of the API.

## Feedback and Improvement

If this package has bought value to your projects, please consider starring it.

## TypeScript REST API (New)

This repository now also includes a TradingView-style REST API and TypeScript client workspace:

- API server: `apps/api`
- Shared parity core: `packages/core`
- TS client package: `packages/client`

Python status:
- Python source is kept for parity fixtures, audits, and regression validation.
- Python is deprecated for new runtime/deployment usage.
- Production runtime should use the ported TypeScript REST API only.

REST coverage now includes:
- Scanner: `POST /api/v1/scan/raw`, `POST /api/v1/scan`
- Symbol search v3 proxy: `GET /api/v1/symbol-search/v3`
- Scanner metainfo proxy: `POST /api/v1/metainfo/:market`
- Snapshot metadata: `GET /api/v1/metadata/fields`, `GET /api/v1/metadata/screeners`, `GET /api/v1/metadata/markets`

Field coverage by asset class (from `apps/api/metadata/fields.json`, generated `2026-02-27`):

| Universe | Canonical fields | Expanded fields (with timeframe variants) | REST metadata route |
|---|---:|---:|---|
| `stocks` | 1003 | 3514 | `GET /api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=stocks` |
| `crypto` | 525 | 3094 | `GET /api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=crypto` |
| `forex` | 439 | 2950 | `GET /api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=forex` |
| `coin` | 518 | 3029 | `GET /api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=coin` |
| `cfd` | 439 | 2950 | `GET /api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=cfd` |
| `futures` | 394 | 394 | `GET /api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=futures` |
| `bonds` | 153 | 180 | `GET /api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=bonds` |
| `bond` | 204 | 204 | `GET /api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=bond` |
| `economics2` | 80 | 80 | `GET /api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=economics2` |
| `options` | 73 | 73 | `GET /api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=options` |

Get complete field list for each asset class from deployed API:

```bash
curl -s 'https://<your-api-host>/api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=stocks'
curl -s 'https://<your-api-host>/api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=crypto'
curl -s 'https://<your-api-host>/api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=forex'
curl -s 'https://<your-api-host>/api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=coin'
curl -s 'https://<your-api-host>/api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=cfd'
curl -s 'https://<your-api-host>/api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=futures'
curl -s 'https://<your-api-host>/api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=bonds'
curl -s 'https://<your-api-host>/api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=bond'
curl -s 'https://<your-api-host>/api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=economics2'
curl -s 'https://<your-api-host>/api/v1/metadata/fields?universe=options'
```

Each returned field object contains:
- `name`: canonical field token for `columns`/filters.
- `displayName`: human-readable label.
- `type`: TradingView field type.
- `variants`: all timeframe/variant tokens for that field.

Deployed API usage vs self-hosting:
- If you only call a deployed API URL, you do **not** need `npm install` in this repo.
- If you run this server yourself, you **do** need `npm install`/`npm ci` and then run build/start scripts.
- If you develop or change this codebase, you need npm for tests, generation, and build.

Production image (Node/TypeScript only, no Python runtime):

```bash
docker build -f Dockerfile.api -t tv-screener-api:latest .
docker run --rm -p 3000:3000 tv-screener-api:latest
```

Run setup:

```bash
npm install
npm run generate:fixtures
npm run generate:metadata
npm run generate:openapi
npm run generate:client:types
npm run test
```

Deep parity and docs audits:

```bash
npm run parity:report
npm run readme:audit
```

Generated outputs:
- `reports/parity-report.json`
- `reports/parity-report.md`
- `reports/readme-audit.json`
- `reports/readme-audit.md`

Migration guide:
- `docs/migration-python-to-ts-rest.md`
- `docs/rest-api-guide.md` (super-detailed REST guide with US + India cookbook, Scanner, Symbol Search v3, Metainfo, cURL + TypeScript examples, filter/filter2 patterns, pagination, and auth/delayed-data usage)
- `docs/python-deprecation.md` (Python retained for parity/audits, deprecated for runtime/deploy use)
